View Article Online View Journal | View Issue -------------------------------------------------- understand the eﬀect of aliovalent doping in Li+ conducting argyrodites, the substitution of P5+ with Si4+ was performed in the solid solutions Li6+xP1xSixS5X. By combining structural characterizations, i.e. X-ray and neutron diﬀraction with elec- trochemical impedance spectroscopy, we show the eﬀect of increasing the Si4+ content on the ionic conductivity. While the larger Si4+ increases the size of the unit cell, it also increases the Li+ concentration and leads to a rising occupancy of Li+ on the transition state for hopping. This additional Si4+ increases the conductivity to greater than 2 mS cm1. This work shows the applicability of aliovalent doping in the superionic argyrodites, thereby demonstrating the optimization potential for this class of materials. 2. Experimental methods Synthesis All preparations and sample treatments for Li6+xP1xSixS5X were carried out under argon atmosphere. Lithium sulde (Li2S, Sigma Aldrich, 99.98%), phosphorus pentasulde (P2S5, Sigma Aldrich, 99%), as well as LiBr (ChemPur, 99.995%) and Si (ChemPur, 99%) were mixed in the appropriate stoichiometric ratio. All precursors were thoroughly dried using a vacuum oven before usage. All mixtures were hand ground in an agate mortar, pressed into pellets and then lled into quartz ampoules (10 mm inner diameter and 10–12 cm in length), which were sealed under vacuum. All ampoules were carbon-coated and pre-heated at 800 C under dynamic vacuum to avoid all traces of water in the reaction atmosphere. The reactions were per- formed at 550 C for two weeks in order to ensure a complete- ness of the reaction and phase purity. The obtained mixture was subsequently ground and isostatically pressed into pellets (10 mm diameter) for the electrochemical measurements or kept as powder for the diﬀraction studies. X-ray diﬀraction Structural investigations were carried out by means of X-ray d diﬀ i i d diﬀ (PANalytical, Netherlands) with Cu Ka radiation (l1 ¼ 1.54051 ˚A, l2 ¼ 1.54433 ˚A) in Bragg–Brentano q–q geometry and a PIXcel3D area detector with 255 measuring channels. Samples were pulverized and placed on (911)-oriented silicon zero back- ground holders that were sealed with Kapton foil under argon atmosphere. Patterns were collected in the range of 10–90 2q with a step size of 0.026 and an exposure time of 100 s per step. Neutron powder diﬀraction High-resolution neutron powder diﬀraction data collection on the argyrodite samples at room temperature was performed in a Debye–Scherrer geometry at the Heinz Maier-Leibnitz Zen- trum (research reactor FRM II, Garching b. M¨unchen, Germany) on the high-resolution diﬀractometer SPODI.53 Data collection using one wavelength was performed, i.e. monochromatic neutrons (l ¼ 1.54817(2) ˚A), and were obtained from the thermal neutron beam at a 155 take-oﬀangle using the (551) reection of a vertically focused composite Ge monochromator of 200 mm in height. The vertical position-sensitive multi- detector (300 mm vertical sensitivity range at 1.117 m sample- to-detector distance) consisting of 80 3He tubes and covering an angular range of 160 2q was used for data collection. The samples (approx. 2 cm3 in volume) were lled into thin-wall (0.15 mm) vanadium cans of 12 mm in diameter under an argon atmosphere and then metal-sealed using indium wire. The vanadium container was then mounted on a capillary spinner enabling sample rotation and thus, minimizing eﬀects of preferred crystallite orientation. Two-dimensional powder diﬀraction data of the continuously rotated sample were collected and corrected for geometrical aberrations and detector nonlinearities.54 Rietveld analysis Rietveld renements were carried out using GSAS II soware.55 Fit indicators – Rwp, Rexp, and c2 – were used to assess the quality of the rened structural models.56 The following i i i ll  d ( ) l f ( ) Fig. 1 (a) Crystal structure of Li6PS5Br. In the ordered structure, Br anions form a face-centered cubic lattice with the free S2 in the tetrahedral sites and PS4 3 in the octahedral voids. In Li6PS5Br, a site disorder between S2 and Br is known as indicated in (b). (b) Li+ positions forming polyhedral cages and a jump path that bypasses a transition state coordinated by the anions. Three diﬀerent jump processes are possible such as the 48h–24g–48h jump, as well as 48h–48h jumps in the cage and between cages. Published on 11 December 2017. Downloaded by POSTECH Library on 1/18/2026 12:12:21 PM. -------------------------------------------------- modeled using a modied Thomson Cox Hastings pseudo Voigt function,57 (4) lattice constants, (5) fractional atomic coordinates, and (6) isotropic atomic displacement parameters. The (7) atomic occupancies of the anions were then allowed to rene simultaneously with all other parameters, to quantify the anion site disorder, while the Si occupancy was xed to the nominal content. Moreover, in the X-ray diﬀraction data the Li occupancies were xed to the values extracted from the neutron renement of Li6PS5Br and the isotropic atomic displacement parameters for Li were xed to 0.05. Finally, (8) phase fractions and the associated lattice parameters of impurity phases were rened. The neutron renements were conducted using the same procedure with several exceptions: (i) the background coeﬃcients were t using a Chebyschev function with 12 parameters and (ii) the Li occupancies and isotropic atomic displacement parameters were allowed to rene. (iii) Additional reections of the vanadium sample holder can be found in the neutron diﬀraction patterns. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy Electrical conductivities were measured by AC impedance spectroscopy, using pellets (1.5 mm thickness, geometric density of all samples 85%) with vapor deposited gold layers. Electrochemical impedance analysis (EIS) was conducted in the temperature range of 20 C to 60 C using a SP300 impedance analyzer (Biologic) at frequencies from 7 MHz to 100 mHz with an amplitude of 10 mV. All measurements were performed in pouch cells under argon atmosphere. Scanning electron microscopy The microstructure of the electrolyte pellets was investigated using the Carl Zeiss Ultra eld emission SEM instrument Merlin. The air sensitive samples were transferred from the glovebox to the vacuum chamber of the SEM with the Leica 3. Results and discussion Structural characterization The Li+ superionic argyrodites Li6+xP1xSixS5Br have been synthesized with increasing Si4+/P5+ ratios in order to study the structural changes and the solubility limit of Si4+ in the struc- ture, as well as to assess the eﬀect of the increasing lithium content on the ionic conductivity. For the structural character- ization, X-ray diﬀraction was performed on all samples. More- over, due to the low X-ray form factor of Li+, selected samples of (x ¼ 0, 0.125 and 0.25) were also investigated using neutron diﬀraction to better probe the changing Li+ substructure. Fig. 2 shows a representative Rietveld renement of an X-ray and a neutron diﬀraction pattern of Li6.125P0.875Si0.125S5Br. All samples exhibit minor impurity phase fractions of Li3OBr and LiBr in the diﬀraction data for the series of solid solutions (see ESI†). The samples seem to react with the ampoules leading to an impurity phase fraction of 2.8 wt% Li3OBr in Li6.125P0.875- Si0.125S5Br, despite the carbon coating and careful drying procedure of the silica ampoules. The minor impurities are unlikely to aﬀect the ionic transport14 and the obtained struc- tural data of all solid solutions, obtained via Rietveld rene- ment against laboratory X-ray and neutron diﬀraction patterns, can be found tabulated in the ESI.† Fig. 3 shows the structural data extracted from Rietveld renements against the laboratory X-ray diﬀraction patterns. With increasing Si4+ content, the lattice parameter of the cubic structure increases linearly until it reaches a saturation level at 30 mol% (x ¼ 0.3) of Si4+ content. The increasing lattice parameter arises from the larger ionic radius of Si4+ (26 pm, tetrahedrally coordinated) on the 4b tetrahedral site, compared to P5+ (17 pm, tetrahedrally coordinated).58 This saturation suggests a solubility limit, aer which a higher content of x ¼ 0.5 does not lead to a further increase in the lattice parameter. With increasing x, an expanding MS4 (M ¼ P1xSix) polyhedral Fig. 2 (a) X-ray and (b) neutron powder diﬀraction data for Li6.125P0.875Si0.125S5Br and the corresponding Rietveld reﬁnements. Shown are the collected data, the proﬁle ﬁt, the proﬁle residuals and the Bragg reﬂections for the main phase (top). A small fraction of the impurity phase Li3OBr (bottom) can be seen in the X-ray diﬀraction pattern, which corresponds to 2.8 wt%. Residual reﬂections in the neutron diﬀraction pattern stem Published on 11 December 2017. Downloaded by POSTECH Library on 1/18/2026 12:12:21 PM. -------------------------------------------------- P fractional occupancies would unequivocally prove the site tion data was not possible. However, the increasing polyhedral volumes and lattice parameters suggest successful incorpora- tion of Si4+ on the P5+ site. It should be mentioned that Ge4+ substitution for P5+ in Li6PS5Br was also attempted; however, no lattice variations were observed, corroborating the negligible solubility of Ge in Li6PS5Br. As mentioned above, the Br anions should be crystallographically separated from the free S2 anions, however a signicant amount of site disorder is known due to the similar ionic radii of the Br and S2 anions.58 Fig. 3c shows the Br/S2 site disorder found in the series of solid solutions, which does not appear to exhibit any major changes with the addition of Si4+. Fig. 4 shows the eﬀect of the Si substitution on the Li+ sub- lattice in Li6+xP1xSixS5Br, as obtained from the Rietveld renement of the neutron diﬀraction patterns. With increasing nominal Si4+ content, the occupancy on the 24g Wyckoﬀposi- tion increases, while the occupancy of 48h position seems to remain constant (with a possible minor decline). It was recently shown that tailoring the anion framework in Li6PS5X by tuning the halide composition (i.e. from Cl to Br and nally to I), and increasing the unit cell dimensions, changes the lithium distribution over these two sites.14 Here, a similar variation is Fig. 4 Structural data of Li6+xP1xSixS5Br obtained from the Rietveld reﬁnements against neutron diﬀraction data. (a) Changing Li+ occu- pancy on the two sites, in which an increasing Si4+ content leads to an increasing 24g occupancy. (b) Li+–Li+ jump distance that shows minor changes in the jump distances. The shown uncertainty reﬂects 3s of Fig. 3 Structural data of Li6+xP1xSixS5Br obtained from the Rietveld reﬁnements of X-ray diﬀraction patterns. (a) Increasing lattice parameters due to the larger ionic radius of Si4+. At a composition of x ¼ 0.3, a solubility limit is reached that is reﬂected by an upper limit in the lattice parameter. (b) Increasing MS4 (M ¼ Si1xPx) polyhedral volumes due to the Si4+ substitution and resultant unit cell expansion. (c) Site disorder between Br and S2, which remains relatively constant with increasing x. The shown uncertainty reﬂects 3s of the Published on 11 December 2017. Downloaded by POSTECH Library on 1/18/2026 12:12:21 PM. -------------------------------------------------- expansion drives additional lithium cations to occupy the transition state of the jump process, i.e. Wyckoﬀ24g. Impor- tantly, besides the lithium occupancy, the jump distances of the diﬀerent Li+ cations can further inuence the diﬀusion as recently shown by Kraet al.14 While changing jump distances were found when altering the anion framework, Fig. 4b shows that the minor structural changes on the cation framework do not signicantly aﬀect the Li+–Li+ jump distances. Ionic transport Temperature-dependent impedance spectroscopy was per- formed on all samples to assess changes to the ionic conductivity. Arrhenius plots of representative samples (x ¼ 0, 12.5, 25 and 50 are shown for clarity), and the corresponding impedance responses, are shown in Fig. 5a and b, respectively. An exemplary t of the impedance data can be found in Fig. 5c. All impedance data were t with an equivalent circuit con- sisting of one parallel CPE/resistor in series with a CPE, rep- resenting blocking electrodes. It should be noted that, due to the low reliability of high frequency data for such fast-ionic conductors, all ts were performed up to a maximum AC frequency of 1 MHz. All impedance spectra exhibit a-values of 0.9, representing the ideality of the CPE,59 and geometric capacitances around 0.1 nF cm2. Additionally, while bulk and grain boundary contributions cannot be de-convoluted, the obtained ideality of the semi-circle and capacitances, as well as the high pellet densities (see scanning electron micrograph in the ESI†), correspond well with bulk transport.60 As seen in Fig. 5b, the impedance of the materials decreases with increasing Si4+ content, which corresponds to an increasing bulk conductivity. Accordingly, the room- temperature ionic conductivities of Li6+xP1xSixS5Br are shown in Fig. 6a. With increasing Si4+ content, the amount of Li+ increases and a three-fold increase in the conductivity from 0.7 mS cm1 for the unsubstituted sample to 2.4 mS cm1 for Li6.35P0.65Si0.35S5Br can be observed. As the Si4+ content is increased further, the conductivity slightly decreases, possibly due to the solubility limit of Si4+ being surpassed and the associated phase segregations. However, the change in carrier density is very small, even for the 30 mol% Si4+ composition. Indeed, a 5% increase in the lithium concentration cannot account for a three-fold increase in the conductivity. The Arrhenius data also provide information on the activa- tion barrier for migration (Fig. 6b). Within the uncertainty in the investigated temperature range, no major changes to the activation energy EA can be seen, even though a changing unit cell size and varying polyhedral volumes are known to aﬀect the conductivity in ionic conductors.10,14 Given that the here-seen changes in the polyhedral volumes are small, it may be possible that the changes in the conductivity may also be related to an additional underlying process. Notably, there are no signicant variations in the site-disorder (see Fig. 3c) that ld i d h h i i b i 14 ibl Fig. 5 (a) Representative Arrhenius ﬁts of the conductivity values for Li6+xP1xSixS5Br obtained from impedance spectroscopy and (b) the corresponding impedance responses at room temperature. (c) Representative ﬁt of the composition x ¼ 0.175 with the employed equivalent circuit. The data were ﬁt until 1 MHz (red data point), providing a high ideality of the process and capacitances in the range of bulk transport (0.134 nF cm2). The apex frequency corresponds to 3.8 MHz. Published on 11 December 2017. Downloaded by POSTECH Library on 1/18/2026 12:12:21 PM. -------------------------------------------------- reason for the increase in the ionic conductivity may be enhanced Li+–Li+ correlation upon adding more Li+ into the 24g site, as seen in the neutron diﬀraction data. The increasing population, and with it the coulombic repulsion, may lead to a correlated motion of ions, as opposed to single unrelated ion jumps. It has recently been shown that correlated motion of ions can benecially aﬀect the ionic conductivity by changing the Haven ratio, and with it the pre-factor, and even the acti- vation barrier for hopping.11 However, a combination of theo- retical calculations, using Ab Initio Molecular Dynamics modelling, as well as Li+ nuclear magnetic resonance experi- ments are necessary to conrm the existence of correlated motion in highly doped argyrodite superionics. Nevertheless, these data show that aliovalent substitution toward the opti- mization of the ionic conductivity in argyrodite superioncs is possible, though more theoretical work is necessary to fully understand the Li+ motion and Li+ interactions in this class of materials. 4. Conclusion In this work, the eﬀect of Si4+ substitution for P5+ in Li6+xP1x- SixS5Br has been investigated as a function of Si4+ content. Using a combination of X-ray diﬀraction, neutron diﬀraction and impedance spectroscopy, it is possible to probe the resul- tant structural changes and elucidate the structure–property relationships within Li-argyrodites when aliovalent substitu- tions are performed. With increasing Si4+ substitution into the structure the lattice parameters increase up to a solubility limit and a three- fold increase in the ionic conductivity can be observed. The structural data show that Si4+ incorporation increases the carrier concentration and polyhedral volumes, while adding more lithium cations into the transition state of hopping. Ultimately, the combination of a changing structure, elevated lithium content and enriched ion interactions lead to an increase in the conductivity, thereby corroborating that improvements to the ionic transport in the class of argyrodites i d d ibl Conﬂicts of interest The authors declare no competing nancial interests. A, 2018, 6, 8th September 2017 0th December 2017 39/c7ta08581h als-a #### troduction ### Effect of Si substitution on the structural and transport properties of superionic Li-argyrodites Nicol`o Minafra, [ac] Sean P. Culver, [a] Thorben Krauskopf, [a] Anatoliy Senyshyn [d] and Wolfgang G. Zeier - [ab] Inspired by the recent interest in lithium ion conducting argyrodites as solid electrolytes for solid batteries, we have investigated the influence of aliovalent substitution in Li6PS5Br. Using Rie refinements against X-ray and neutron diffraction, coupled with impedance spectroscopy, we mo the influence of Si [4+] substitution for P [5+] in Li6+xP1�xSixS5Br on the structure and ionic trans properties. A step-wise incorporation of Si [4+] leads to an expansion of the unit cell, as well as inclusion of additional Li [+] within the structure. The increasing Li content occupies the struc transition state and, in combination with the structural changes, leads to a three-fold improveme the ionic conductivity. This work demonstrates that the argyrodite material class can be optim through aliovalent substitution, thereby making argyrodites an ideal system for studying solid electro within the field of solid-state batteries. conductors (or solid electrolytes) have recently gained interest due to their possible use in solid-state Using a fast Li [+] conducting solid provides the possireplace the ubiquitous liquid electrolytes, hopefully - safer and more reliable batteries.
